Places Visited

Misty Rain Tower 235

— Qian Taisheng

On the birthday of the lotus flower, Jiaxing, this city in the corner of the southern lake, all the people in the city, all the farmers in the countryside, from the small merchants in the county to the fashionable ladies and female students, from every road around the city to every small river in the countryside, everyone is like attending a grand banquet, like going to an ancient market. They bring some cash with them, wear new clothes, and rush to the Misty Rain Tower, the "South Lake" with its misty waves and shimmering waters.

Early in the morning, the boat ladies who park their boats on the edge of the streets and markets put rouge on their lips, wear fragrant flower water, and go to the Xuan Gong Bridge and Xin Ma Road to wait for their first customers of the day in their boat cabins. In the countryside, the sky is barely bright, and those proletariat crowds take the watermelons from their melon fields, bring their wives and children, and row to the city in their bare boats in the faint morning light.

The day before, small merchants and the leisure class who sit in teahouses ordered silk net boats from Wuxi and booked a sumptuous banquet in advance, preparing to play a loud flute and sing Kunqu opera with three cups of "Gaoliang wine" in the evening breeze of the South Lake.

At the East Gate, small ferry boats are parked on every riverbank, lined up neatly, close to the bank. The public ferries, which have raised flags especially for today, are parked at designated docks, flying white bamboo cloth flags with black characters.

The temporary public ferries for bare boats also raise flags, pulling people on the shore and shouting.

Under the dark iron foreign bridge, the public ferries are carrying full boats of people. The pretty ferry ladies, standing at the bow of the boat and shouting the number of passengers, often turn around to make a few crude jokes to the passengers in the cabin. The wind on the water and the powder on their faces, black with white, are actually praised by the passengers as "black roses" in this small city!

Boat after boat, large silk net boats, small ferry boats, and bare boats, the people on the boats use bamboo poles and oars to touch the water surface and row through the water. The wind of summer floats on the water surface. Passing the small Misty Rain Tower, the classical oriental Misty Rain Tower, surrounded by green, and a bright South Lake are reflected in front of them.

The Misty Rain Tower, this classical building surrounded by water and green gardens, an oriental building, with a pavilion, a hall, some rockeries, corridors, small pavilions, a small lotus pond, a small bridge, and the fresh, sweet, and tender South Lake water chestnuts are produced on all sides.

The four gardens on the lakeside are tightly packed with large boats and small boats. Boat after boat of guests jump down from the boats. Inside, they include women who have been refined by the urban soul with rouge, powder, and perfume. Black, green, soft silk and soft yarn, long and narrow-waisted cheongsams reveal fleshy arms. There are also figures in silk shirts, white straight pants, and so-called double-paid young masters, students; small merchants; still fluttering in white summer cloth long shirts and Indian silk Hangzhou silk wide trousers; small shop friends and clerks, wearing white short shirts and trousers, squeezing in the crowd, devouring line powder, mung bean soup, dried bean curd, and watermelons. Women who are slightly prettier naturally have a group of young and brave bodyguards protecting them, and the funny sound of spring chasing in the autumn wind wafts through the air.

The sound of flutes rings on the lake, and Kunqu opera spreads from the boats on the water.

White awnings, green small foreign boats, white clothes, shadows of women, four oars, hitting the water surface, and the sounds of harmonicas and silk strings faintly come through. People are still coming boat after boat, but the sky is gradually turning into night.

The lights are lit at the head of the Misty Rain Tower, illuminating the bright water surface. In the small ferry boats and the large silk net boats, the autumn wind blows coolly, and the shallow smiles on the eyebrows, corners of the eyes, and lips of the women under the night lights!

Free Discussion

The Yellow River's Waters Come from Heaven 236

— Cao Juren

That great poet of the Tang Dynasty left the famous line, "The Yellow River's waters come from heaven." What can we do about that? We can only do our best and await fate. If it wants to meander from the north to who-knows-where in the south, we can only let it have its way. Wasn't the Snake King reborn this year? The breaching of the Yellow River must be the will of Heaven. Throughout history, only this line of poetry has truly captured the essence of the Yellow River; Li Qinglian truly deserves to be called the Poet Immortal.

The "await fate" school of Yellow River experts – the Free Talk section doesn't have enough space for me to trace their lineage. The historical records are insufficient, and some parts don't connect. However, regarding "river conservancy labor, prefectures and counties extract it from the Lijia system, with the Lijia assessing corvée labor based on wealth. If a family hires five laborers, the monthly cost is ten taels of gold, depleting their wealth and leaving them destitute. When the laborers arrive at the worksite, they demand everything, causing many to flee. Summons are issued to hire replacements, incurring the same expenses again. Officials only have the name of recruiting laborers, while the harm falls on the families of those nominally hired, and the benefits go to the supervisors of the works." (Memorial of Chen Yingfang, a secretary in the Ministry of Rites during the Wanli period of the Ming Dynasty.) This approach of relying on the Yellow River's fate has been passed down through the generations and continues to this day. Historical records show that from July of the second year of the Jiaqing reign to August of the twenty-fourth year, the Yellow River breached its banks seventeen times. In the thirteenth year alone, it breached three times. In just the thirteenth and fourteenth years of Jiaqing, the cost of repairing and blocking the southern breaches exceeded forty million taels. River officials engaged in "rampant embezzlement, and the expenses were incalculable; aside from military expenditure, this was a major item."

Having "awaited" fate, it's time for the "do your best" school to step up. This school venerates the Great Yu as their founding ancestor. After the Great Yu, there are the Jia Rang school and the Wang Jing school. Jia Rang's three policies for governing the river emphasized not competing with the river for land, "Now, implementing the best policy, relocating the people of Ji Province who are in the path of the water, breaching Liyang, diverting harmful floods, and directing them northward to the sea... Using the funds spent on river management over several years to provide livelihoods for the relocated people; once this is accomplished, the river will be stabilized and the people will be at peace." The Wang Jing school's methods were the opposite of Jia Rang's, advocating for suppressing floods, claiming to have realized this from the words "spread" and "unite" in the Yu Gong's description of "spreading into the nine rivers, uniting into a counter-flowing river." Generally, from the Eastern Han Dynasty onwards, there were the Jia school of not competing for land and the Wang school of suppressing floods in river management policies. After the Jia school was implemented for a period, the Yellow River's waters still came from heaven, so they switched to the Wang school; after the Wang school was implemented for a period, the Yellow River's waters still came from heaven, so they switched to the Jia school again. However, the historians always said that by using a certain school, the Yellow River's waters did not come from heaven many times, to show that human effort should be exhausted.

In the fifteenth year of the Shunzhi reign, the river breached at Shanyang; in the first year of the Kangxi reign, the river breached at Yuanwu and Xiangfu; in the sixteenth year of the Kangxi reign, the river overflowed in all directions. Jin Fu was appointed Director-General of River Conservancy, and Jin Fu created the method of storing clear water to combat the yellow water, and using water flow to scour the sand. However, the Governor Gan Chenglong said that the lower river should be dredged, not retained, and heavy embankments should be retained, not built, which disagreed with Jin Fu's opinion. At that time, the officials supported Jin Fu's proposal, but the Kangxi Emperor sided with Gan Chenglong, and the embankment construction faction was defeated. Generally, the embankment construction faction and the anti-embankment construction faction exhausted their human efforts for the Kangxi Emperor. By the Jiaqing period, they awaited fate. In the fifth year of the Xianfeng reign, the river breached at Tongwaxiang, and it meandered to the north again!

Now, haven't the Yellow River's waters come from heaven again? Exert human effort? Await fate? Exert human effort and await fate? Therefore, throughout history, only Li Qinglian's poem has captured the essence of the Yellow River. Besides the Jia and Wang schools, a Li school should be established.

On the Literary Scene's Leader 237

— He Ru

There are both methods and books on ascending the literary dragon. I say that today's literati all consider themselves geniuses and look down on others as incompetent. If people are compared to fish and dragons, then everyone is a fish, and they consider themselves divine dragons. How can there be so many dragons? A group of dragons without a head is the phenomenon of today's literary scene. Who is the head dragon, it seems, still awaits a genuine genius. Genius, genius, I truly seek it day and night. During the long summer days, I write this essay on the literary scene's leader.

At the end of the Eastern Han Dynasty, the court was in chaos, and the principles of conduct collapsed. Li Ying alone upheld moral integrity and elevated himself with his reputation. Scholars who were received by him were said to have ascended the Dragon Gate. Prince Zhanghuai of the Tang Dynasty commented that it was a metaphor using fish. The Dragon Gate is the mouth of the river, located in Longmen County in present-day Hezhou. The "Sanqin Records" by Xin Shi states that the River Ford is also known as the Dragon Gate. The water is dangerous and impassable, and no fish or crabs can ascend it. Large fish from the rivers and seas gather below the Dragon Gate by the thousands, but cannot ascend. Those who ascend become dragons. The term "ascending the dragon" originates from this. The reason why Li Ying could become the leader was that he was concerned about the country, loyal and public-spirited, had a pure heart and hated evil, made dangerous and profound arguments, did not hide from the powerful, stood up bravely, did not shirk from disaster, and was a model for the world, the chieftain of the partisans. Does the literary scene of today have such a person? Are there those who encourage themselves with this?

During the chaos of the Eight Kings and the Five Barbarians, internal stabilization and external defense were not achieved. Literati were distressed, and pure conversation was valued. Wang Yan was skilled in abstruse discussions, captivating the people of the time. The court and the public unanimously called him the Dragon Gate of the generation. Later scholars all admired and imitated him. It can be seen that Wang Yan was also written as the leader among the literati. I have often discussed this. Wang Yan's pure conversation was not a great evil. It should not be considered as farting, farting, how could this be true? However, he was fond of arcane emptiness, believed in inaction, and held an important position, yet he claimed not to be involved in worldly affairs. Therefore, he caused countless people to be misled and Shi Le blamed him for destroying the world. Does the literary scene of today have such a person? Are there those who can be slightly compared to him?

During the Qi and Liang dynasties, Ren Fang had a great literary reputation. He liked to associate with and promote others. Scholars and friends who were praised by him were often promoted. He always had dozens of guests at his seat. People at the time admired him and called him Lord Ren, comparing him to the three lords of Mengchang. Later scholars such as Liu Xiaochuo, Lu Chui, Dao Qian, Zhang Lü, Liu Xian, Liu Bao, and Yin Dan all came from his school. People at the time called it the Dragon Gate Gathering, or the Orchid Terrace Gathering. The so-called "gathering" is like saying a gathering today. The so-called Dragon Gate Gathering and Orchid Terrace Gathering are the names of literary gatherings at Ren Fang's residence, like literary tea parties today. As for those like Liu Xiaochuo, they hoped that Ren Fang would recommend them and use this to get promoted and make a fortune. Ren Fang was not only good at writing, but also excelled at taking notes. He could also share people's worries and enjoy their happiness. He was able to be the leader of the literary scene for a time. Today's rich people have never lacked those who attach themselves to elegance and seek to dominate the literary scene. Let me ask, does the literary scene of today have such a person as Ren Fang? Are there those who can seem to be slightly similar?

Alas! If genius does not appear, what will happen to the literary scene? Don't say that there is no one who is the head dragon, just be happy that there are methods to ascend the dragon. How lucky am I to be a member of today's literati!

Reading "On Continuing a Work": Another Explanation for Mr. Cao Juren 238

— Qiu Zhushi

Mr. Cao said two important things in "On Continuing a Work": first, for the sake of society's undertakings, continuing a work is not only harmless, but sometimes necessary, such as with "history;" second, literary creation is inherently social, so it is no different from historical works which need to be continued, such as the Water Margin. I extremely agree with the first point, but I cannot but disagree with the second point.

The task and nature of history are different from that of literature. It is a scientific thing. As long as the viewpoints and methods are the same, it is okay for a history to be continued or collaborated on by not just one or two people, but by dozens, hundreds, or even thousands of people. What about literary works? As Mr. Yu Pingbo said, "There are no good continued books (Note: referring to literary books). It is not necessarily that the talent and sentiment of the person continuing the book is far inferior to that of the predecessor, but because the talent and personality are different, just like their faces, forcing them to conform will only hurt both."

A "correct" point of view is necessary for literary works to be great and permanent. The same theme can have completely different results when written by two people with different points of view. If someone with a different point of view from the author of the previous work continues the work, even if it is not a "dog's tail continuing a sable," wouldn't it be "a bull's head not matching a horse's mouth?" Moreover, the themes taken for the continuation may not be exactly the same as those of the previous work? Then the result will confuse the readers and make them not understand what is going on.

Secondly, a "unique" style and a "special" tone are also important for literary works to be great and permanent. Let us assume that the point of view of the continuer is exactly the same as that of the previous author, but if the style and tone cannot be consistent, the continuation is still futile. The failure of the continuation of Dream of the Red Chamber (such as Continuation of Dream of the Red Chamber) is due to this, and the failure of the continuation of Water Margin (such as Conquering the Bandits) is also due to this.

Again, Mr. Cao said, "Since ancient times, everyone has participated in the work of creation in the chanting of ballads and the telling of stories. It is almost impossible to know who is the creator and who is the continuer. The Water Margin can only be said to be the joint creation of thousands and millions of people over hundreds of years since the Southern Song Dynasty. Even today, storytellers in Oriental bookstores are still doing the work of continuing the work." There is a grammatical error here. The singing of ballads through the ages is an addition and modification, not a continuation. The telling of stories is also an addition and modification, not a continuation. Only at the end is it written down and becomes the current state, such as The Peacock Flies Southeast, Mulan Ci, and various "bianwen," stories of Xu Wenchang, etc. Water Margin is different from these. Water Margin is neither a continuation nor an addition and modification, but a creation. (Mr. Cao has never failed to recognize this point, so he said that "The Water Margin can only be said to be the joint creation of thousands and millions of people over hundreds of years since the Southern Song Dynasty," but he suddenly turned around and said, "Even today, storytellers in Oriental bookstores are still doing the work of continuation," this is where the problem lies.) Although Water Margin, like the telling of stories, has undergone many years and many people's addition and modification, but the addition and modification is only a pile of materials. These materials must be chosen and forged by the heart and eyes of the author, and re-expressed with the author's own pen according to the author's point of view, before it becomes Water Margin, just as a writer obtains materials from real society to write literary works, hence it is called creation. Only in this way is the author's skill very important to the quality of the work. Try comparing Romance of the Three Kingdoms and Water Margin. Although they are both based on the materials that have been told, the literary value of each is very different, then you can know. Although the Romance of the Western Chamber has materials from Zhao Delin's Shang Ji, "The whole village sings Cai Zhonglang" (Note: the blind old man's lyrics are used), after all, it is not a continuation. Homer's epic, according to one school of thought, the meaning of "Homer" is "a collector of scattered fragments," then it can be further proved from Western facts that ballads and stories can be added, modified, written down, or created, and negate Mr. Cao's so-called continuation.

Originally, it was Mr. Cao "throwing a brick to attract jade, asking Mr. Qi Fan to talk about it again," but now it has become my tile coming to make a fool of myself.

Note: The original text is "The whole village listens to Cai Zhonglang."

Miscellaneous Talks from Mountain Living 239

— A Ying

(1) Idle People and Idle Matters

"Xia Wei Duan Die" says:

Wang Can liked donkeys and kept several at home, some of which were worth as much as a hundred gold. One was called "Fallen Hairpin," the second was called "Distant Journey," the third was called "Blue Bird," the fourth was called "White Phoenix," the fifth was called "Facing the River," the sixth ... the seventh was called "Running Lightning," and the eighth was called "Flying Star."

According to this, Wang Can kept at least eight donkeys, and these donkeys also had very pleasant names, some fragrant and seductive, some beautiful, some majestic, and some ethereal. Because of Wang Can's donkeys, I thought of golf, which is most popular with my family's young marshal. Everyone who breathes the air of a metropolis probably knows the tension and busyness of metropolitan life. However, when you occasionally get a chance to run into a golf course, you will feel that in the metropolis, there are also so many idle people of ancient times, pushing the ball into the distant hole, and have to push eighteen small ball fields and eighteen holes. It is natural to push a ball into a hole once, but it is said that it is also very common to push more than sixty times and not push a ball into a hole. A circle comes over, one or two hours, or one night, will waste you. Such a life is really worthy of the idle life of the leisure class, which is more elegant than Wang Can. When a friend took me to see it, he told me that this thing is no longer new in the United States. He did not say the reason why it is not new. I think this can be inferred. First, the thing should be constantly renewed to be interesting. Second, perhaps eighteen holes are not enough to waste. The thing that you want to consume when you have nothing to do has a broad future, so will the golf course with thirty-six holes, which is twice as many, be realized in the near future? However, from here, I see the decadence of the hopeless life of the declining class. (To be continued)

Woman (1) 240

— Shen Congwen

(Autumn, like spring in autumn.)

On the third-floor passageway of a certain hospital, a young nurse wearing a white cap and a white robe, carrying a small white porcelain basin, walked hurriedly from the east corridor to the west. When she reached the stairs, a greeting stopped her footsteps. A woman came up from the second floor, swirling on the wide zigzag stairs, wearing a green robe and holding a most fashionable vermilion leather wallet, giving people a feeling of "red amid green." The woman had a pair of long legs, making her walk very lightly when going upstairs. She was about twenty-seven or eight years old. Because the decoration was legal, it seemed that her age could be reduced a little. However, in the medical field, the marks made by time on this person cannot be concealed by artificial methods. That smile written on the corners of her mouth and between her eyebrows, and her demeanor, already carried a tune of "a beauty arriving late."

She could not be said to be very beautiful, but her eyebrows and eyes were delicate and refined, and her manner was generous and noble. Her body was well-proportioned, and the clothes she wore were very flattering, and precisely because of the late spring demeanor of "red amid green," she left a good impression on people that was not easy to forget after the first meeting.

Since she had been coming to the hospital on time this month to see a patient, she was very familiar with the nurse. Now, seeing the nurse by the stairs, she greeted her and quickly ran upstairs.

She said to the nurse in a kind and gentle voice:

"Miss Xia, how are you!"

The nurse smiled and looked at the vermilion leather wallet in the hand of the person who called her.

"Miss Ru, how are you!"

"Miss Xia, when did the doctor say the patient will be discharged?"

"Dr. Zeng said that he would be better in a week, but Mr. Mei himself said this morning that he wanted to leave."

"Leave today?"

"That's what he said."

The woman in green did not speak and passed the wallet from her right hand to her left.

The nurse in white seemed to understand what that meant, but then said:

"Dr. Zeng said, 'No.' If he doesn't sign, Mr. Mei cannot be discharged."

The door of a certain ward at the west end of the passageway opened, and a man in white with a shaved head showed half of his body and shouted to the nurse in the passageway:

"Miss Xia, come here quickly!"

The nurse said softly, "I'm not coming quickly!" She made an unhappy expression with her eyebrows and hurried away. Miss Ru stood by the stairs for a while, not leaving immediately. She saw a young, round-faced girl, holding a large light blue flower in her hand, supporting a young and handsome man, slowly walking downstairs. The man looked like he had just recovered from a long illness, his face pale, with a smile on his face, while the girl's face was bright and rosy, extremely happy.

A pair of beautiful and lively eyes watched the two people walking down the stairs in a zigzag pattern, until their shadows disappeared and were obscured by the screen at the stairwell. These beautiful eyes then stopped on the brown grass mat by the stairs, which was a small blue flower.

Recent Overview of New Cotton Crop in Shandong Province 250

(Eastern Shandong) Areas along the Jiaoji Railway, north and south of the Yellow River, specializing in fine velvet cotton, such as Binzhou, Putai, and Lijin, produce approximately 200,000 "dan" annually. It does not reach Jinan but is transported to Qingdao via the Zhangdian Station on the Jiaoji Railway. Therefore, there are very few cotton merchants in Jinan. There was heavy rain on the 30th, with about 80% of the expected rainfall.

(Southern Shandong) Cotton produced in areas such as Caozhou Prefecture is mainly coarse velvet, and the quantity is small. It is not shipped to Jinan but is only used locally for making wadded quilts. In recent years, local products have suffered drastic declines. Farmers, due to the high price of cotton, planted 10-20% more this year than last year. Last year, Shandong produced approximately 600,000 bales of cotton, which were traded in Jinan. The cotton produced in Binzhou, Putai, and Lijin in Eastern Shandong is not included in this figure. According to the heavy rain on the 23rd of the 7th lunar month, all areas in Shandong received moisture. However, areas that had not received rain for a long time, such as Wuqiao and Ningjin in Northern Shandong, benefited greatly. On the other hand, areas such as Gaotang and Xiajin in Western Shandong experienced a sudden reduction in production due to the heavy rain on the 30th. New cotton will be available around the beginning of the 7th lunar month. (End)

Grain Biao Flour Plummets then Slightly Recovers 253

丨Factories Intend to Maintain Prices丨

After the opening of the flour market yesterday, various months showed signs of initial flatness followed by increased demand. Prices for imported wheat, Chicago, and Canada were down slightly by one to three "jiao". Sentiment was flat after the opening price. However, in subsequent trading sessions, outside shorts covered their positions, and factories both sold and bought. As a result, the market declined sharply but then gradually recovered after that decline, improving by one "fen" compared to the lowest point of the day. When the afternoon market opened, due to repeated new lows on the market, factories considered maintaining prices, and the market atmosphere improved again. However, actual sales to customers remained weak, and factory inventories continued to increase daily. This type of sharp decline followed by a slight recovery cannot be predicted. As a result, the current month was better by two and a half "fen" compared to the previous day, September/October were better by two "fen" and two "li" and a half, December was better by two "fen", and January was better by seven and a half "li".

丨Afternoon Flour Market Recovers, Bulls Cover丨

Yesterday, after the opening of the wheat futures market, prices for various months were down slightly by one to three "jiao" due to imported wheat prices. Moreover, market sentiment was shrouded in a pessimistic atmosphere. Therefore, market sentiment was extremely uneasy after the opening price. Discussions

"So-So" 262

— Wen Bing

"So-so," in the grand scheme, explains the entirety of the decline of national character; in the smaller scheme, it explains an individual's lack of progress in life.

This is not a case of being unwilling to do something or simply folding one's sleeves and not doing it. Because this is a word used to "cut off" or dismiss a certain event, it clearly indicates that one had engaged to some degree. So one cannot say that there was no initial intention to improve; one can only say that one performed perfunctorily, without the courage to be thorough, to the point of failing midway and then dismissing it with a "so-so."

Examining the origin of "so-so," it's nothing more than difficulty and timidity.

A certain matter, from beginning to end, from attempt to success, inevitably, the process is fraught with many hidden difficulties. Breaking through these difficult points allows one to reach the end, to reach success; otherwise, one stops before the turning point and inevitably sighs, "So-so, let's just leave it at that."

So "difficulty" is the first formidable enemy of "so-so."

However, difficulty is just difficulty, and it can ultimately be conquered. As the saying goes, "Nothing is difficult in the world for one who sets his mind to it," and "Difficulty is the lighthouse of success," succinctly explaining that "success depends on human effort." However, this human effort ultimately requires a courage of perseverance and indomitable spirit; only then can one break through the difficult barriers. If one is timid and does not advance, the result will inevitably be "so-so."

So "timidity" is the second formidable enemy of "so-so."

During the late Qing Dynasty, the Treaty of Livadia failed with Russia, but it was later restored through negotiations by Marquis Tseng. This alone monopolized the glory of diplomatic history. His father, Zeng Guofan, was able to recover half of the country that had been seized by the Taiping Heavenly Kingdom by training local militias. Both of these men bravely overcame difficulties and never resorted to "so-so." (The fact that Zeng Guofan was enslaved by the Manchus but did not harbor misguided notions of nationalism is another matter.)

In this day and age, there are many difficult things, but few brave people. From high officials to commoners, all are huddled under the smokescreen of "so-so," unable to extricate themselves.

Looking at any individual, ask him how his work is going, and the answer will almost always be, "So-so."

Page 20

In reality, there are indeed many people who are unwilling to tackle difficult tasks. For those things that they are willing to do, if they encounter difficulties, they change direction, turn around, and ignore them.

On another level, "so-so" is even more a crime of empowering the strong, oppressing the weak, and burying justice. In any matter, one can disregard whether either side is in the right or wrong; the first word that must be brought out is "so-so." Only by saying it once and I saying it again can the matter be smoothed over. The result is that the strong prevail, the weak are held by the nose and unable to breathe, and justice cries out.

Even the idle friends in the alleys, happily kicking over a peddler's load of vegetables, always have a third party chime in with a few "so-so" to settle the matter.

"So-so" is like this: It is the great enemy of successful endeavors and the upholding of justice. To put it more bluntly, because of "so-so," what is done is equivalent to not being done. Mediating the affairs of others means serving as a helper for the strong.

Three Major Reasons for Women Remaining Single 263

— Shi Bin

Women are also members of the populace, and the importance of their position needs no further elaboration! Since the founding of the Republic of China, influenced by European and American trends and guided by domestic pioneers, women themselves have become aware of the loss of their human rights over the past several thousand years and the urgent need to restore them. As a result, slogans and banners advocating equality between men and women suddenly became popular throughout the country. This has led many women with shallow knowledge, who only understand the term "equality" but not its actual meaning, to stray onto the wrong path, needlessly adding countless complications to an already weak nation! And what is the result? Their actions and wills have attracted the criticism and attention of society, who believe that modern women are too liberated and too unbridled! Little do they know that there is a group of women that you don't pay attention to, but who are very worthy of attention, and who are hidden in a corner of society? This is what this article is about: "Single Women." Based on our thorough investigation and multifaceted research, we know that they are definitely not unmarried because of broken hearts or old-fashioned marriages. They have a special psychology and feeling. After my many times of careful consideration! After many efforts, I have decided the reasons for their being single, and I will record them below:

(1) Fear Now that women's demands for liberation are increasing, some men are very enthusiastic to help them (?). The only way they help is by talking about love; and what is their psychology? It is either changing allegiance in the morning and evening, or abandoning them after the initial affair; there are also some so-called benevolent gentlemen, who put on another mask, and will do the trick of marrying again and again, even if their children are already in groups, they still want a divorce; such things, to the parties involved, may not be a big deal, but to the general women with compassion and rationality, they think this is an act of losing their minds and burying their reason; there is a sigh of "nothing in the world is more than this"! Therefore, they see through the men and think that they are all like this, and fundamentally begin to doubt, and then from doubt arises "fear," this concept of fear, in their minds, the more imprinted the more profound, the more profound and more solid! (2) Observation In the past, women only lived in the family, and their knowledge was not wide; now it is not the case, they mingle with men in the society together, they can directly and indirectly, or see and hear, all the unfortunate events that occur for the sake of marriage, and finally everything ends up being the loss of women; and she looks around at her friends after marriage, 19 are not satisfied, some are resentful because of family troubles, some are sad and indignant because their husbands do not cooperate; they "observe" the pain of others, on the one hand, she is gladly celebrating that she has not yet been involved in the vortex, on the one hand, she is trying to avoid all the marriage leads.

(3) Backing In the past, China seemed to have no share for women, everything was exclusively occupied by men; they were not allowed to study, and they were not allowed to work outside; they had no other way to think of anything except relying on men; so the quality of their fate was shifted with the men. Even if they suffered all kinds of oppression and injustice, they could only bow their heads and endure. Now the environment is very different! Everything has a share for women, once they run from the narrow family to the broad society, it is like releasing a group of caged birds, return me to freedom; in their newly felt feelings, they have aroused unlimited interest in their hearts, and have a stable career, doing "backing," in the material is both happy to deposit and use, in the spirit is free; comfortable and natural, those self-proclaimed women who see through the world's affairs, they look at marriage. It's like asking them to enter hell, steadfastly unwilling!

The above three reasons are all related to each other and occur, but the latter is the most important, this contagious unmarried doctrine, has now been a great echo; they deeply believe in admiring, the advanced life of the unmarried, and deeply sad about the family life of trouble and constraints, so the women who tend to this doctrine, are increasing day by day, but not decreasing:

Finally! I have to say one more sentence: most of the single women are knowledgeable, they are capable, thoughtful, if applied to the family, then the family organization, children's education, will certainly contribute more; unfortunately, they do not care about the overall situation, it really affects the society a lot: alas! 22, 8, 6, drafted in Meng Lou

Clerk Communication

A Huge Sum of Money 264

Editor Sir:

I am an apprentice in a small cigarette paper grocery store; the store sells various domestic cigarette papers such as Golden Mouse Brand and Beauty Brand every day, and the number is very considerable. In each small packet of these domestic cigarettes, there is a small card with exquisite printing and advertisements on the back. But I see that most of the people who buy cigarettes always throw this small card on the ground and rarely pay attention to it. I think this huge amount of printing money, isn't it completely throwing money into the water? Why not save this money and buy two fighter planes from the United States? Usually, you can write some advertisements on these planes; its power may be much greater than the current small cards! I want to find a way to get the domestic cigarette company to adopt this suggestion.

Sir, can you agree with this approach? Can you help me to publish this letter in the clerk communication column of your newspaper's local supplement? Sincerely, Yu Zhiqing

Editor Yu Jun's suggestion is indeed a practical and feasible approach. We know that every domestic cigarette company with a slightly higher status, such as Nanyang Huacheng and other companies, spends at least 40,000 to 50,000 yuan on these small cards every year; if you concentrate it, the amount is really considerable. The effectiveness of this small card is undoubtedly very weak because 90% of them are discarded. If the companies uniformly save it, it will definitely not affect the business. Wasn't the Red Tin Package (non-domestic product) implemented the year before last because of the soaring cigarette prices? As a result, its sales are still increasing. What's more, transfer this money to save the country? I think smokers will definitely not object. The authorities of domestic cigarette companies! You might as well consider it?

Drama

War and Peace (8) 266

— Ling He

Scene 1: Life and Death

Old man: Isn't that right? In the past, when it was this time of day, the old monk would ring the bell. Even dozens of miles away, you could hear it. People outside would definitely hear the bell and lead their mules home. Every hot night, everyone would come here to cool off, talking and laughing. But the world really changes fast. Not long ago, this place completely changed. Of course, this is also the luck of our village. Look, even the big tree that is more than 50 years old has suddenly died. It's really God's will.

Old woman: Alas! No one comes to light a candle all year round, and even the Bodhisattva doesn't bless us anymore.

Middle-aged C: It's useless to talk about the past. It's getting dark, and I've finally lost hope for my livestock again. I'd better go back. (Exit)

Wounded soldier A: Why hasn't the big brother who went to get the straw come back yet? I really want to lie down for a while.

Middle-aged B: Then I'll help you in first. He'll probably be here in a while. (He helps wounded soldier A up. The old man also hurries forward to help.)

Wounded soldier A: No need, no need, grandpa! You're so old, how dare I ask you to serve me? I can still walk.

Middle-aged A: (Carrying straw) Huh? Did they leave? Ah! You're still here. (Points to wounded soldier D)

Old man: No, the other one went in first and is waiting for your straw. Send it in quickly, spread it out, and then carry this big brother in. (Middle-aged A enters the temple)

Wounded soldier D: Thank you so much, I didn't expect you to treat us so well.

Old man: Don't be polite, "Rely on your parents at home, and rely on your friends when you're away," "There's nowhere in life that you won't meet"!

(Middle-aged B comes out of the temple) Look, this big brother is getting polite, he says you treat him too well.

B, this counts as... We common people are risking our lives, can't we even do this little thing? We are all common people, we were originally like a family.

Old woman: Soldiers like you who understand the truth are good soldiers. I have to go back, I won't accompany you. They will come to carry you in later. (Exit, but immediately comes back.) I'm really sad. The one who grabbed me and called me mom just now was really pitiful. Now he's being shaken so badly in the rickshaw, I don't know... It's good to say it's not bad; I don't know if he's still okay. I'm afraid there's no one left.

Middle-aged B: Who knows? That military doctor is really hateful, if he hadn't run fast, I would have wanted to beat his mother to death.

(Middle-aged A comes out carrying a piece of broken board. Calls to B to carry wounded soldier D in.)

Voice: ...Run! ...They're coming.

Old woman: What is it again? (Soliloquy)

Voice: Run! Everyone get out of the way! (From noisy to gradually clear.) ...The soldiers are coming

Old woman: Oh! God, the soldiers are coming again

(She runs in a panic, but immediately shouts loudly.) Run! Soldiers, soldiers are coming, Japanese soldiers are coming! (Exit)

Middle-aged A: (Comes out of the door.) Are the Japanese soldiers coming? Ah! The Japanese soldiers are coming... (He asks loudly into the distance) Are they Japanese soldiers? Are they really Japanese soldiers?

Voice: Run quickly, the soldiers are coming...

Old man: (Following behind middle-aged B comes out of the door.) What's going on?

Middle-aged B: Are they really Japanese soldiers?

Middle-aged A: (Preparing to run) Who knows. They just shout soldiers. No matter what, let's go.

Old man: Then what about the wounded soldiers here?

Movie Supplement

Poverty in the American Film Industry 267

— Hou Feng

In the history of American film art, we cannot find the changes in artistic trends like those in Germany. Expressionist films and Romanuc films are unique to Germany. American films can be said to have no content at all. We can review the content only when art has progressed and changed; but with American films that have no content, this review is very difficult. What is the degree of evolution from the golden age of silent films to the current rise of sound films?

The American film industry can be said to be at the extreme of poverty and exhaustion. The unprecedented economic recession has directly affected the film audience, and the number of moviegoers in each cinema is much less than before!

Of course, the so-called golden age of art is the era when food, clothing, and shelter are satisfied. If food, clothing, and shelter cannot be satisfied, where is the need for artistic effort? However, people with sufficient economic means feel out of place with art; what they need is the curvaceous beauty of women, so the reason why Revue dance films are popular lies in this point.

Art originally often arises when artists are poor. However, this is personal poverty, not the poverty of the times. When the times are poor, there is absolutely no good work produced. Moreover, film is not a personal art. In this storm-like world panic, hoping for good artistic film works to appear is just a dream.

Major companies such as Paramount, Warner Brothers, Metro, and Fox have all been swept into the vortex of economic panic, causing some to reduce their executives and others to save expenses, all focusing on implementing reorganization. At the same time, to open up this situation, they are not using good artistic works but using entertaining and interesting works to grasp the social trend. This is the recent situation in the American film industry. The era of war and economic panic has no possibility of producing true art. Film is one of the five major industries in the United States, and in this period of sharp economic panic, it cannot escape the scope of this panic.

Film producers who lack accurate feelings, no matter how hard they try to create art, are ultimately impossible. Their conscience has already been lost. They can only offer some ordinary and tasteless films without artistic value to the American moviegoers who have forgotten criticism.

The American film producers' flood-like release of films with ordinary tastes and fierce violence is a ruthless aspect of 1933 and a stain on the history of film art. Revue films originally disappeared for a while, and we thought this was a deformed child of the early stage of sound films. However, recently, the voices of praise for Revue films in the American film industry can be said to be soaring to the sky, "24ND Suet" is the product they are praising like crazy.

Let's compare the United States with Germany and Italy! Germany, in the suffering of the World War, produced expressionist films and its reactionary historical drama films, while the United States, in the predicament of this economic fear, only has Revue films, sexy and interesting films.

In short, the American film industry is probably no longer able to produce true art!

Film Review

Review of "Murders in the Zoo" 268

— Bai Liang

丨Great Light Projection丨

After watching "Murders in the Zoo," I can tell the audience who come later without hesitation:

(1) If you have great hope for this film, hoping that it will make some new contributions to society, then you will definitely be disappointed and extremely frustrated.

(2) If you want to understand the actual life of society from this film, then it is still possible, because it can show you a layer of the current society. Moreover, this layer is the most beautiful layer.

(3) If you originally regarded watching any film as a pastime after dinner: then, I am not saying anything excessive, I can responsibly tell you that you can get a lot. Because this story is as moving and as true as its title; there are hand-to-hand combats between people, fights between animals, human wails, and animal roars. When you tell this story to others, you can definitely sincerely move many listeners, you can scare your children to run away, and you can scare your lover into hiding in your arms.

Speaking of the subject matter of this story, it is undoubtedly exposing the evils and ugliness in the most beautiful layer of current society. Naturally, some people will never believe that such things as evils and ugliness can happen in the most beautiful layer of current society, especially in the so-called upper class: but, the fact is the fact, not to mention in foreign countries, in our old China, for the compradors, landlords, gentry, officials and other classes under the current system, in order to achieve some kind of despicable desire of theirs, there are many who are working hard to create various kinds of evils all day long? This is something that no one can hide from anyone. The screenwriter of our "Murders in the Zoo" has firmly grasped this point. He powerfully depicts an animal scholar who occupies a very high position in society. In order to monopolize his love for his wife, he does not hesitate to use very sophisticated scientific methods to kill all the love rivals who are close to his wife. As a result, although he was killed because of this, the screenwriter's main point is impossible to conceal anyway.

As for the director, sound recording, and lighting, they can all be said to be very good. In terms of actors, the insidious and resolute attitude of Lionel Alwill, who plays the animal scholar, and the lively and true expression of his wife, Kathleen Burke, can be said to be successful. Looking at the whole film, it cannot be regarded as a film with high appreciation value among the films of the same type that the United States has transported to China in the past. However, if we hope that movies can take on a cultural mission, then this film does not seem to be what the public needs.

A Critique of "The Pirate" 269

— Moore

Broadly speaking, "The Pirate" is still a film about the romantic entanglements of men and women, ending with the typical happy marriage. However, "The Pirate" differs from American-style romance films. Its story is a tragedy imbued with a sense of sorrow. Shikov, while privately in love with Mary Carroll, also falls into a romantic relationship with the Indian girl, Dina. But due to the friendship with Mackoff, the lover of Mary, he wanders the world, becoming a pirate. This kind of youthful Wertherian spirit, though foolish, is indeed very moving. Later, his union with Mary is merely due to Mary's deep affection; calling it love is more like gratitude. This type of story is rarely seen in American films.

At the same time, "The Pirate" also has its significance in its interpretation of religion. It is skeptical of "God," but believes that "faith" is necessary. This incomplete view of "religion" can represent a section of European figures. Naturally, surrounded by the tradition of Christianity, it can only attack other "divine religions" (Indian ones). It would be incorrect for viewers to assume that his attack on "Indian divine religions" is a protection of "Christianity." The subtitle, "If you have a spirit, I will go to the church to pray to you," the phrase "If you have a spirit," I think should be emphasized.

Technically, the director doesn't seem to have the power to control the story, especially emotionally. I feel that emotional scenes, which the director fails to fully grasp and portray, are a great failure. Furthermore, after Shikov becomes a pirate, the director's use of "sudden violence" to express the trauma to his soul is very good. However, in moments of solitude, there should be scenes and expressions of loneliness and sorrow because simply writing about "violence" is not enough. Also, when Shikov is torn between "friendship" and "love," the director should use every means to express his pain. To put it extremely, the most dramatic part of "The Pirate" lies in this area, which the director of "The Pirate" neglected.

In terms of acting, the male lead can act, but the director cannot allow him to give his best performance. The female lead has far fewer opportunities to act, so it's natural that she doesn't deliver a particularly outstanding performance. Other aspects, such as camera angles and scene divisions, are worth seeing. In short, "The Pirate" is not a particularly outstanding film. But compared to American films, whether in terms of story or technique, it is still acceptable.

Film Critics and Producers 270

— Shen Xiling

Some friends in film production say: "Today's film critics only care about their own opinions and strict demands; they never pay attention to the difficulties of production. If they were to produce a film themselves, I believe it would be a mess." At the same time, some friends in film criticism say: "Today's Chinese films, in every aspect, are crude and immature..."

They both have their reasons, but they haven't fully understood or have overlooked the divisions and connections between them. In reality, critics do overlook the objective conditions of production. But producers shouldn't necessarily force critics to produce a film themselves. The producer's task is to explore his creativity and achieve his grand creations. The critic's important task is to illuminate the inherent meaning of a work and its value. To do this, he must know all the objective conditions of production and the knowledge of social sciences.

In order to seek the source of his creation, the producer can at least receive some clues from the critic, and at least some directional inspiration. Of course, he must also use his clear mind to distinguish the accurate path among the various criticisms. Critics and producers each have their own paths of self-cultivation. Furthermore, the progress of Chinese cinema does not lie in mutual ridicule but in mutual encouragement.

Japanese Cinemas in Shanghai 271

— Chengda

丨The History and Content of the Towa Hall丨

At a time when Sino-Japanese relations are very "close," it seems that the Japanese film industry should also be worthy of our attention. I will now briefly describe the situation of Japanese photography halls (cinemas) in Shanghai. About four or five years ago, there was a Japanese cinema (I forgot the name) located near the Shanghai Grand Theater on North Sichuan Road. Because it was small and did not select films well, it soon closed down. However, the "Towa Hall," which has a history of decades, still exists. It can be said that it has become the only Japanese cinema in Shanghai today. Five years ago, it was located on Wuchang Road in Hongkou; now it has moved to the intersection of Zha Pu Road and Haining Road. The style of the entrance is not grand, but the interior is purely "Japanese-style" and extremely refined in its decoration. Upstairs and downstairs can accommodate two or three thousand spectators; however, the upstairs is reserved for female guests, with no seats but a thick cushion spread on the floor, low in the front and high in the back, divided into three levels. Each level is surrounded by a copper railing so that they can lean against the railing while sitting on the floor. There are also women downstairs. Tickets are priced at six cents downstairs and one yuan upstairs. There are no daytime screenings, only one screening at night, except on Sundays. There are many viewers, but soldiers and students receive a 50% discount on tickets. The films they show can be divided into "new" and "old." "New" refers to contemporary works, and "old" refers to historical films in ancient costumes, all with profound consciousness, and the techniques are absolutely not crude. The subtitles are aesthetic, very elaborate, and today they also show many sound films. Good silent films are of course not abandoned, and are shown occasionally. During the screening, men and women stand beside the stage and recite simple dialogue according to the scenes in the film, so that the general audience can fully understand, which is an innovation that no other country has. The theater is commercially operated, so there is no prohibition on saying "only nationals are allowed in," but in fact, foreigners rarely go to Japanese cinemas.

Film Novel

Murderous Revenge and Devoted Love: STRANGE RHAPSODY 272

— Dake

Upon hearing a word from his wife, Du Sheng immediately pushed open the window and shouted downstairs! "You madmen, come on in!" He hurriedly put on his clothes, went downstairs and opened the door, and the crowd surged into Du Sheng's house. They said in unison, "We've come to say goodbye. We received an emergency order to depart for the front lines at dawn tomorrow." Du Sheng stepped forward, expressing sincere emotion, and patted Qisa on the shoulder, saying, "Really?" Qisa said, "Really, we're taking the train early tomorrow morning."

The Gypsy orchestra of Ji Jinxixi suddenly started playing music. A young officer in the crowd, Jiao San Heli, stared at Elena on the staircase, and everyone saw her. Elena said happily to them, "Good evening, or good morning. Welcome to have supper, or breakfast. San Heli bowed and said, "We only need to see you and we are happy." Someone said, "It wouldn't hurt to have some wine." Everyone echoed and laughed. Du Sheng then led the way, shouting in front, "Those who want to drink, come this way, there's plenty of wine here for you to drink." They filed in and entered Du Qian's dining room. They cheered and drank freely until the east turned fish-belly white and the first light of dawn shone through the windows. But their enthusiasm showed no sign of waning.

Elena secretly slipped out and ran into the large living room, pressing her hand to her eyes, deeply feeling the fatigue and dullness of life. And Qisa came in. He also called her over and said, "You haven't said two complete sentences to me tonight." Qisa said, "That's because we are together." Elena said with a smile, "This kind of place where everyone gathers feels like everyone is conspiring to prevent us from talking. Don't you think it's strange!" Qisa said, "This is called being near yet far, people's intentions are distant." Elena continued, "Inside the same room, you are on the east side, and I am on the west side, separated by many people's shoulders and strangely shaped heads, isn't it like being separated by layers of peaks?" Qisa said, "If I were to shout loudly to you, 'Hey, you with the most beautiful eyes, I want to be with you,' I don't know what kind of changes would occur in those strangely shaped heads." Elena gently embraced Qisa and quietly reprimanded him, "Then you don't need to shout like that. Haven't I already heard the voice in your heart?"

As they were talking in such a gentle and tender way, the Gypsy music outside continued to play. Qisa sighed, saying that Du Sheng and Elena had treated him so well these past few months, and now the time of joy was coming to an end. Elena said sadly, "If I had known this earlier, why didn't I..." (To be continued)
